{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01VnMKNELQP9FWFSGR8UxE37","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01MhAi544d9rUQAUyF2iFLP4","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is the core subsystem in Envoy that processes HTTP requests from downstream clients through upstream dispatch, response delivery, and back to clients. It is a complex orchestration of multiple interdependent components that work together to:\n\n1. Accept raw network bytes from downstream connections\n2. Decode HTTP frames using protocol-specific codecs (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3)\n3. Execute a chain of filters that can inspect, modify, or intercept the request\n4. Route the request to an appropriate upstream cluster\n5. Manage upstream connections and retry logic\n6. Encode the upstream response back to the downstream client\n\nThis document explains how the four primary components of the HCM interact to achieve this goal.\n\n---\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: The Central Request Orchestrator\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc) is the top-level filter in Envoy's network filter stack. It implements:\n\n- **Network::ReadFilter** — receives raw bytes from the downstream connection\n- **ServerConnectionCallbacks** — receives callbacks from the HTTP codec when new streams are created\n- **Network::ConnectionCallbacks** — manages the lifecycle of the underlying TCP/TLS connection\n- **Http::ApiListener** — allows direct HTTP request injection (for API listeners, not socket-based)\n\n### Key Responsibilities\n\n1. **Codec Management**: Creates and maintains an HTTP codec (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, or HTTP/3) lazily or on-demand. The codec is protocol-agnostic internally; ConnectionManagerImpl treats it as a black box that decodes bytes into HTTP frames and encodes HTTP frames back to bytes.\n\n2. **Stream Lifecycle**: For each incoming HTTP request, creates an `ActiveStream` object that wraps the stream and manages its state from arrival through completion. These streams are organized in a linked list for efficient management during connection shutdown or drain.\n\n3. **Filter Chain Creation**: When a new stream arrives, delegates to `FilterChainFactory` to create the per-stream filter chain (detailed below).\n\n4. **Connection-Level Concerns**:\n   - **Drain Decisions**: Monitors connection drain signals and prevents new streams on draining connections (graceful shutdown)\n   - **Overload Management**: Checks with `OverloadManager` to decide whether to accept new connections\n   - **Watermark-Based Flow Control**: Propagates buffer watermark events from the underlying connection to all active streams to manage memory usage\n\n5. **Stream Completion**: When a stream finishes, ensures proper cleanup, logging (via access loggers), and deferred deletion to avoid lifetime issues.\n\n### ActiveStream: Per-Stream State Wrapper\n\n`ActiveStream` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h, lines 141–end of private section) is a critical internal struct that:\n\n- Wraps a single HTTP request/response pair\n- Owns the `FilterManager` that executes the filter chain for this specific stream\n- Implements `RequestDecoder` to receive decoded HTTP frames (headers, data, trailers)\n- Implements `FilterManagerCallbacks` to encode responses back downstream\n- Maintains stream-specific state: headers, trailers, reset reasons, tracing spans, stream info\n\nThe lifecycle of ActiveStream:\n\n1. **Creation**: When the HTTP codec detects a new request (via `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream`), ConnectionManagerImpl creates an ActiveStream.\n2. **Filter Chain Execution**: The stream's FilterManager iterates through decoder filters as request data arrives (headers → data → trailers).\n3. **Response Path**: Once upstream sends a response, it flows back through encoder filters in reverse order.\n4. **Completion**: After response is fully encoded, the stream calls `completeRequest()`, logs access logs, and is marked for deferred deletion.\n\n### Codec Instantiation Strategy\n\nThe codec is created lazily:\n- **For HTTP/1.1 and HTTP/2**: On the first call to `onData()` (arrival of first byte from client)\n- **For HTTP/3**: On `onConnection()` (connection initialization)\n- **For API Listeners**: Caller must explicitly call `createCodec()`\n\nThis deferred instantiation reduces memory overhead for connections that never receive data.\n\n### Connection Shutdown and Drain\n\nConnectionManagerImpl maintains a `NetworkReadFilter` contract to receive `onNewConnection()` when a connection arrives and `onData()` when bytes arrive. During drain:\n\n1. New streams are not created (request returns 503 Service Unavailable)\n2. Existing streams are allowed to complete gracefully\n3. The underlying TCP connection remains open until all streams finish\n\n---\n\n## 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain: Request Processing Pipeline\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`FilterManager` (source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc) is the per-stream filter chain execution engine. It orchestrates the flow of request and response data through a configurable chain of filters, managing iteration state, buffering, and filter communication.\n\n### Filter Chain Structure\n\nFilters are organized in two ordered lists:\n\n#### Decoder Filters (Request Path: A → B → C)\nWhen configured as:\n```\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: A\n  - name: B\n  - name: router (terminal, sends upstream)\n```\n\nRequest flow: **A.decodeHeaders** → **B.decodeHeaders** → **Router.decodeHeaders** → **A.decodeData** → **B.decodeData** → **Router.decodeData** → **A.decodeTrailers** → **B.decodeTrailers** → **Router.decodeTrailers**\n\n#### Encoder Filters (Response Path: C → B → A, Reverse Order)\nResponse flow: **Router.encodeHeaders** → **B.encodeHeaders** → **A.encodeHeaders** → **Router.encodeData** → **B.encodeData** → **A.encodeData** → **Router.encodeTrailers** → **B.encodeTrailers** → **A.encodeTrailers**\n\nThe reverse order on the response path allows filters to \"unwrap\" responses in the opposite order they wrapped requests, maintaining symmetry (similar to middleware pattern in other frameworks).\n\n### Filter Wrapper Classes\n\nFilterManager wraps each filter in an `ActiveStreamFilterBase` subclass that manages iteration state:\n\n1. **ActiveStreamDecoderFilter** (filter_manager.h, lines 240–325)\n   - Wraps a `StreamDecoderFilter` (user-implemented filter)\n   - Maintains decoder-specific state and iteration control\n   - Implements `StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks` to provide filter callbacks (e.g., `continueDecoding()`, `sendLocalReply()`)\n\n2. **ActiveStreamEncoderFilter** (filter_manager.h, lines 330–end)\n   - Wraps a `StreamEncoderFilter`\n   - Manages encoder-specific state\n   - Implements `StreamEncoderFilterCallbacks`\n\nBoth inherit from `ActiveStreamFilterBase` which provides:\n- **Iteration State Management**: Tracks whether filter iteration is Continue, StopSingleIteration, or StopAll (with buffering)\n- **Filter Callbacks**: Connects each filter to the FilterManager for callbacks\n- **Status Handling**: Interprets filter return codes (FilterHeadersStatus, FilterDataStatus, etc.) and decides whether to continue or stop iteration\n\n### Filter Status Return Codes\n\nFilters return status codes that control iteration:\n\n| Status | Decoder Behavior | Encoder Behavior |\n|--------|------------------|------------------|\n| **Continue** | Iterate to next filter | Iterate to next filter |\n| **StopIteration** | Stop headers iteration; call `continueDecoding()` to resume | Stop headers iteration; caller must continue |\n| **StopAllIterationAndBuffer** | Stop all iteration and buffer following data until `continueDecoding()` | Stop all and buffer |\n| **ContinueAndDontEndStream** | Continue headers iteration but don't end stream (filter will inject data later) | — |\n\nWhen a filter returns `StopIteration`, the iteration state is recorded, and subsequent data frames call the same filter again rather than advancing to the next filter. Only when the filter calls `continueDecoding()` does iteration advance.\n\n### Filter Factory and Chain Creation\n\n`FilterChainFactory` (envoy/http/filter_factory.h) is invoked once per stream by ConnectionManagerImpl. It:\n\n1. Calls each filter factory function in order\n2. Each factory creates a filter instance and calls `addDecoderFilter()` or `addEncoderFilter()` on the callbacks object\n3. FilterManager appends these to its `StreamDecoderFilters` and `StreamEncoderFilters` lists\n\nThis allows dynamic filter creation based on route configuration, listener configuration, or other runtime state.\n\n### Data Buffering and Watermarks\n\nWhen a filter returns `StopAllIterationAndBuffer`:\n\n1. FilterManager allocates a buffer for subsequent data\n2. All subsequent data is appended to this buffer\n3. The filter is responsible for calling `continueDecoding()` or `continueEncoding()`\n4. When iteration resumes, the buffered data is replayed through the filter chain\n\nWatermarks prevent unbounded buffering:\n- If buffered data exceeds a configured limit, the connection signals high watermark\n- The upstream (or filter) is expected to slow down sending data\n- If high watermark is not respected and buffer exceeds hard limit, a 413 or 500 error is sent\n\n---\n\n## 3. Router Filter: Request Routing and Upstream Dispatch\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe Router Filter (`source/common/router/router.h/cc`) is the terminal decoder filter—it is always the last filter in the decoder chain. Its responsibilities are:\n\n1. **Route Selection**: Consult the route configuration to select a target cluster and route entry\n2. **Host Selection**: Use the cluster's load balancer to pick an upstream host\n3. **Connection Pool Allocation**: Obtain an HTTP connection pool from the ClusterManager\n4. **Upstream Request Creation**: Create and manage `UpstreamRequest` objects\n5. **Retry Logic**: Automatically retry failed requests based on route configuration\n6. **Timeout Management**: Set and enforce per-try and overall request timeouts\n7. **Shadow Routing**: Optionally send a copy of the request to a shadow cluster for testing\n8. **Hedged Requests**: Optionally send duplicate requests to different hosts for faster response\n\n### Route Selection\n\nWhen `Router::decodeHeaders()` is called:\n\n1. Extract route information from the request (headers, method, path, query parameters)\n2. Match against the configured `RouteConfiguration` (provided by RDS — Route Discovery Service)\n3. Retrieve the matching `RouteEntry` which specifies:\n   - **cluster**: The upstream cluster name\n   - **timeout**: Per-try and global timeout settings\n   - **retry_policy**: Conditions that trigger retries\n   - **shadow_policy**: Whether to shadow the request\n   - **weighted_clusters**: Alternative clusters to route to (canary deployments)\n\n### UpstreamRequest Lifecycle\n\nOnce a route is selected, the Router creates an `UpstreamRequest` object (source/common/router/upstream_request.h/cc):\n\n1. **Creation**: `std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>()` with a reference to the Router (parent) and a `GenericConnPool` from the ClusterManager.\n\n2. **Header Forwarding**: Router calls `acceptHeadersFromRouter()` on UpstreamRequest, which:\n   - Modifies headers (adds x-envoy headers, removes hop-by-hop headers)\n   - Passes the modified headers to the UpstreamRequest's internal `UpstreamFilterManager`\n   - The last filter in the upstream chain, `UpstreamCodecFilter`, attempts to encode headers to the upstream codec\n\n3. **Body Forwarding**: Subsequent `decodeData()` calls forward body data to UpstreamRequest\n\n4. **Upstream Connection Pool**: When the first header is forwarded, UpstreamRequest requests a connection from the pool. The ClusterManager allocates or reuses an existing HTTP connection pool.\n\n5. **Upstream Codec Bridge**: The `UpstreamCodecFilter` (source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.h/cc) maintains a `CodecBridge` that connects the upstream stream (from the upstream codec) back to the downstream FilterManager's encoder phase. When the upstream sends response headers, they are passed through the upstream filter chain (in reverse), then to the downstream encoder filter chain.\n\n6. **Retry Logic**: If the upstream connection fails or returns a retriable error (5xx status, connection reset), and `retry_policy` allows, Router creates a new UpstreamRequest and retries.\n\n7. **Completion**: When upstream sends trailers (end of response), UpstreamRequest signals completion. Router's encoder filters encode the response headers and body back downstream.\n\n### Router Filter Extensions\n\nRouter is itself extensible:\n\n- **Upstream HTTP Filters**: Similar to downstream filters, but run on the upstream request/response stream\n- **Shadow Writers**: Custom implementations can decide where to send shadow traffic\n- **Load Balancer Selection**: Through the cluster's load balancer interface\n\n---\n\n## 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity: Connection Pool Management\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ClusterManagerImpl` (source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h) manages all upstream clusters and their connection pools. It provides:\n\n1. **Cluster Registration**: Manages static clusters from the bootstrap config and dynamic clusters from CDS (Cluster Discovery Service)\n2. **Connection Pool Allocation**: Allocates HTTP/TCP connection pools per cluster per thread\n3. **Load Balancer Management**: Maintains load balancer instances per cluster\n4. **Health Checking**: Coordinates health checks and outlier detection\n5. **Thread-Local Storage**: Maintains thread-local cluster state for lock-free access\n\n### Connection Pool Architecture\n\nWhen Router calls `ClusterManager::httpConnPool()`:\n\n1. **Pool Lookup**: ClusterManager looks up a connection pool for the specified cluster, priority level, and protocol version\n2. **Pool Creation**: If no pool exists, it allocates one:\n   - For HTTP/1.1: `Http1ConnPool` (source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.h/cc)\n   - For HTTP/2: `Http2ConnPool` (source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.h/cc)\n   - For HTTP/3: `Http3ConnPool` (source/common/http/http3/conn_pool.h/cc)\n3. **Pool Callback**: Router registers itself as a connection pool callback\n4. **Connection Allocation**: When Router attempts to get a connection, the pool:\n   - Checks for idle connections in its internal pool\n   - If none available, allocates a new physical TCP/TLS connection\n   - Returns a handle to the connection\n\n### Load Balancing\n\nThe ClusterManager holds a reference to each cluster's load balancer. When Router needs a host:\n\n1. Creates a `LoadBalancerContext` containing:\n   - Request headers (for header-based routing)\n   - Upstream transport socket options\n   - Retry count (for retries)\n2. Calls `LoadBalancer::chooseHost(context)` to get an upstream host\n3. The load balancer applies:\n   - Health checks (unhealthy hosts are excluded)\n   - Outlier detection (hosts with too many errors are ejected)\n   - Load balancing algorithm (round-robin, least request, ring hash, etc.)\n   - Locality awareness (prefer hosts in the same zone/region)\n\n### Health Checking and Outlier Detection\n\nClusterManagerImpl integrates with health checking infrastructure:\n\n- **Health Checkers**: Each cluster can have multiple health check configurations (HTTP, TCP, gRPC)\n- **Outlier Detection**: Automatically ejects hosts that produce too many errors\n- **Load Balancer Integration**: The load balancer is notified when a host's health status changes, immediately removing unhealthy hosts from consideration\n\n### Cluster Discovery Service (CDS)\n\nClusters can be static (in bootstrap config) or dynamic (from CDS). ClusterManagerImpl:\n\n1. Maintains a CDS subscription via `CdsApi` (source/common/upstream/cds_api_impl.h/cc)\n2. When clusters are discovered, creates new Cluster objects and integrates them\n3. When clusters are updated, re-initializes connection pools and load balancers\n4. When clusters are removed, gracefully drains existing connections\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Request Through the System\n\n### Downstream Request Path\n\n```\n1. Network bytes arrive on TCP/TLS connection\n   ↓\n2. ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()\n   → Codec::dispatch() to decode bytes into HTTP frames\n   ↓\n3. Codec calls ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()\n   → ConnectionManagerImpl creates ActiveStream\n   → FilterChainFactory creates filter chain\n   → FilterManager is initialized\n   ↓\n4. Codec calls RequestDecoder::decodeHeaders()\n   → ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()\n   → FilterManager::decodeHeaders()\n   → Iterates through decoder filters: A → B → Router\n   ↓\n5. Codec calls RequestDecoder::decodeData()\n   → FilterManager::decodeData()\n   → Flows through same filter chain\n   ↓\n6. Codec calls RequestDecoder::decodeTrailers()\n   → FilterManager::decodeTrailers()\n   → Router is now at end of stream\n   ↓\n7. Router::decodeHeaders() selects route and cluster\n   → Obtains UpstreamRequest and GenericConnPool from ClusterManager\n   → Selects host using LoadBalancer\n   → Forwards headers to UpstreamRequest\n   ↓\n8. UpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter()\n   → Modifies headers (adds x-envoy headers, adjusts timeouts)\n   → UpstreamFilterManager processes upstream filter chain\n   → UpstreamCodecFilter encodes to upstream codec\n   → Codec connects to upstream host\n   ↓\n9. Upstream connection established\n   → Codec encodes headers to upstream\n```\n\n### Upstream Response Path\n\n```\n1. Upstream codec receives response headers\n   ↓\n2. UpstreamCodecFilter::CodecBridge::encodeHeaders()\n   → Response flows back through UpstreamFilterManager (reverse order)\n   → UpstreamRequest signals Router via decodeHeaders callback\n   ↓\n3. Router::encodeHeaders() is invoked\n   → Encoder filters iterate in reverse order: Router → B → A\n   → Each encoder filter can modify or inspect response\n   ↓\n4. Response data flows upstream → downstream\n   → UpstreamCodecFilter receives data from upstream\n   → Router forwards to ActiveStream::encodeData()\n   → FilterManager iterates encoder filters\n   ↓\n5. Response trailers arrive\n   → Same flow through encoder filter chain\n   ↓\n6. FilterManager::encodeTrailers() completes\n   → Codec encodes all response data to downstream connection\n   ↓\n7. Downstream receives full response\n   → ActiveStream marks stream complete\n   → AccessLogger is invoked\n   → Stream is deferred-deleted\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points: Where Users Extend Envoy\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\nUsers implement `StreamDecoderFilter` or `StreamEncoderFilter` (envoy/http/filter.h) to:\n\n- Inspect or modify request/response headers\n- Inspect or modify request/response body\n- Perform authentication/authorization\n- Add tracing\n- Implement custom routing logic (via `sendLocalReply()` to terminate early)\n- Buffer and delay streams\n\nFilters are registered via the filter factory pattern and instantiated per stream.\n\n### 2. Upstream Filters\n\nSimilar to HTTP filters, but apply to the upstream request/response. Used for:\n\n- Modifying upstream-specific headers\n- Compression/decompression\n- Custom upstream request/response handling\n\n### 3. Load Balancer Implementations\n\nUsers implement `LoadBalancer` (envoy/upstream/load_balancer.h) to:\n\n- Implement custom load balancing algorithms (consistent hashing, power-of-two, etc.)\n- Use custom routing criteria from request context\n- Integrate with external load balancing services\n\n### 4. Health Checkers\n\nUsers implement health check plugins to:\n\n- Perform custom health checks (application-specific protocols)\n- Integrate with external health check systems\n\n### 5. Cluster Types\n\nUsers implement `Cluster` (envoy/upstream/cluster.h) to:\n\n- Define custom cluster behavior (aggregate multiple endpoint sources, etc.)\n- Implement custom endpoint discovery mechanisms\n\n### 6. Access Loggers\n\nUsers implement `AccessLog` (envoy/access_log/access_log.h) to:\n\n- Log detailed request/response information\n- Send logs to custom destinations (metrics systems, log aggregators)\n- Trigger alerts based on response codes or latency\n\nAccess loggers are invoked when a stream completes and have access to:\n- All request headers, body, trailers\n- All response headers, body, trailers\n- Duration, bytes sent/received, status codes\n- Cluster info, upstream host info\n- Custom stream-specific state (filter state)\n\n### 7. Filter State\n\nFilters and custom code can store arbitrary state in `StreamInfo::FilterState` (envoy/stream_info/filter_state.h) for:\n\n- Passing data between filters\n- Making data available to access loggers\n- Sharing custom context across the request lifecycle\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Codec Errors\n\nIf the downstream codec encounters a malformed HTTP message:\n\n1. Codec reports error via `ServerConnectionCallbacks::onCodecError()` or similar\n2. ConnectionManagerImpl sends a 400 Bad Request response (or closes connection)\n3. Stream is terminated and cleaned up\n\n### Filter Errors\n\nIf a filter encounters an error and calls `sendLocalReply()`:\n\n1. FilterManager stops iteration of remaining filters\n2. Encoder filters are still executed to allow them to modify the error response\n3. The local reply (error) is encoded to the downstream connection\n4. Stream completes with error status\n\n### Upstream Connection Errors\n\nIf the upstream connection fails during request forwarding:\n\n1. UpstreamRequest detects connection reset or timeout\n2. Router's retry logic consults `retry_policy`\n3. If retriable, creates new UpstreamRequest with incremented retry count\n4. Selects new host via load balancer\n5. If all retries exhausted, sends 503 or upstream error response\n\n### Timeout Errors\n\nTwo levels of timeouts:\n\n1. **Per-Try Timeout**: Timeout per attempt to reach upstream. If exceeded, triggers retry if configured.\n2. **Global Timeout**: Total time allowed for request (across all retries). If exceeded, sends 504 Gateway Timeout.\n\nBoth timeouts are managed by UpstreamRequest and Router, using the Event Dispatcher's timer mechanism.\n\n### Stream Reset\n\nIf a stream is reset mid-processing (client disconnect, filter error):\n\n1. ActiveStream::onResetStream() is called\n2. Any pending UpstreamRequest is cleaned up\n3. Downstream encoder is stopped\n4. Stream is deferred-deleted\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files Reference\n\n### Core Connection Management\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` — ConnectionManagerImpl class, ActiveStream struct\n- `envoy/router/rds.h` — Route discovery service interface\n\n---\n\n## Summary: Component Interactions\n\nThe four major components interact as follows:\n\n1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** receives raw bytes and creates an HTTP codec. When a new HTTP stream is detected, it instantiates an **ActiveStream** and delegates to **FilterChainFactory** to build the filter chain.\n\n2. **FilterManager** iterates through the decoder filter chain as request data arrives. Filters can modify, inspect, or stop iteration.\n\n3. **Router Filter** is the terminal decoder filter. It selects a route from the **ClusterManager**, creates an **UpstreamRequest**, and begins forwarding the request.\n\n4. **ClusterManager** provides connection pools and selects hosts via load balancers. It manages the lifecycle of upstream connections.\n\nThe response flows back through **UpstreamRequest** (which runs upstream filters), then through **ActiveStream** (which runs downstream encoder filters), and finally the **Codec** encodes the response bytes to the client.\n\nThroughout this process:\n- **Filters** at any stage can send local replies to short-circuit the chain\n- **Status codes** control iteration behavior (continue, stop and buffer, etc.)\n- **Timeouts** and **retries** are managed by the router\n- **Access loggers** are invoked when the stream completes\n- **Custom state** can be stored in FilterState for cross-filter communication\n\nThis architecture enables Envoy's flexibility: users can insert custom filters at any point, implement custom load balancers, extend codec behavior, and integrate custom health checks—all without modifying Envoy's core request processing loop.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3995,"cache_read_input_tokens":44815,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3995},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2a7af225-dd84-47b1-ab85-97c77251293e","uuid":"d05f6c2f-0d2f-4b04-b395-ec5574d23e88"}

It is a complex orchestration of multiple interdependent components that work together to:\n\n1. Accept raw network bytes from downstream connections\n2. Decode HTTP frames using protocol-specific codecs (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3)\n3. Execute a chain of filters that can inspect, modify, or intercept the request\n4. Route the request to an appropriate upstream cluster\n5. Manage upstream connections and retry logic\n6. Encode the upstream response back to the downstream client\n\nThis document explains how the four primary components of the HCM interact to achieve this goal.\n\n---\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: The Central Request Orchestrator\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc) is the top-level filter in Envoy's network filter stack. It implements:\n\n- **Network::ReadFilter** — receives raw bytes from the downstream connection\n- **ServerConnectionCallbacks** — receives callbacks from the HTTP codec when new streams are created\n- **Network::ConnectionCallbacks** — manages the lifecycle of the underlying TCP/TLS connection\n- **Http::ApiListener** — allows direct HTTP request injection (for API listeners, not socket-based)\n\n### Key Responsibilities\n\n1. **Codec Management**: Creates and maintains an HTTP codec (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, or HTTP/3) lazily or on-demand. The codec is protocol-agnostic internally; ConnectionManagerImpl treats it as a black box that decodes bytes into HTTP frames and encodes HTTP frames back to bytes.\n\n2. **Stream Lifecycle**: For each incoming HTTP request, creates an `ActiveStream` object that wraps the stream and manages its state from arrival through completion. These streams are organized in a linked list for efficient management during connection shutdown or drain.\n\n3. **Filter Chain Creation**: When a new stream arrives, delegates to `FilterChainFactory` to create the per-stream filter chain (detailed below).\n\n4. **Connection-Level Concerns**:\n   - **Drain Decisions**: Monitors connection drain signals and prevents new streams on draining connections (graceful shutdown)\n   - **Overload Management**: Checks with `OverloadManager` to decide whether to accept new connections\n   - **Watermark-Based Flow Control**: Propagates buffer watermark events from the underlying connection to all active streams to manage memory usage\n\n5. **Stream Completion**: When a stream finishes, ensures proper cleanup, logging (via access loggers), and deferred deletion to avoid lifetime issues.\n\n### ActiveStream: Per-Stream State Wrapper\n\n`ActiveStream` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h, lines 141–end of private section) is a critical internal struct that:\n\n- Wraps a single HTTP request/response pair\n- Owns the `FilterManager` that executes the filter chain for this specific stream\n- Implements `RequestDecoder` to receive decoded HTTP frames (headers, data, trailers)\n- Implements `FilterManagerCallbacks` to encode responses back downstream\n- Maintains stream-specific state: headers, trailers, reset reasons, tracing spans, stream info\n\nThe lifecycle of ActiveStream:\n\n1. **Creation**: When the HTTP codec detects a new request (via `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream`), ConnectionManagerImpl creates an ActiveStream.\n2. **Filter Chain Execution**: The stream's FilterManager iterates through decoder filters as request data arrives (headers → data → trailers).\n3. **Response Path**: Once upstream sends a response, it flows back through encoder filters in reverse order.\n4. **Completion**: After response is fully encoded, the stream calls `completeRequest()`, logs access logs, and is marked for deferred deletion.\n\n### Codec Instantiation Strategy\n\nThe codec is created lazily:\n- **For HTTP/1.1 and HTTP/2**: On the first call to `onData()` (arrival of first byte from client)\n- **For HTTP/3**: On `onConnection()` (connection initialization)\n- **For API Listeners**: Caller must explicitly call `createCodec()`\n\nThis deferred instantiation reduces memory overhead for connections that never receive data.\n\n### Connection Shutdown and Drain\n\nConnectionManagerImpl maintains a `NetworkReadFilter` contract to receive `onNewConnection()` when a connection arrives and `onData()` when bytes arrive. During drain:\n\n1. New streams are not created (request returns 503 Service Unavailable)\n2. Existing streams are allowed to complete gracefully\n3. The underlying TCP connection remains open until all streams finish\n\n---\n\n## 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain: Request Processing Pipeline\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`FilterManager` (source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc) is the per-stream filter chain execution engine. It orchestrates the flow of request and response data through a configurable chain of filters, managing iteration state, buffering, and filter communication.\n\n### Filter Chain Structure\n\nFilters are organized in two ordered lists:\n\n#### Decoder Filters (Request Path: A → B → C)\nWhen configured as:\n```\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: A\n  - name: B\n  - name: router (terminal, sends upstream)\n```\n\nRequest flow: **A.decodeHeaders** → **B.decodeHeaders** → **Router.decodeHeaders** → **A.decodeData** → **B.decodeData** → **Router.decodeData** → **A.decodeTrailers** → **B.decodeTrailers** → **Router.decodeTrailers**\n\n#### Encoder Filters (Response Path: C → B → A, Reverse Order)\nResponse flow: **Router.encodeHeaders** → **B.encodeHeaders** → **A.encodeHeaders** → **Router.encodeData** → **B.encodeData** → **A.encodeData** → **Router.encodeTrailers** → **B.encodeTrailers** → **A.encodeTrailers**\n\nThe reverse order on the response path allows filters to \"unwrap\" responses in the opposite order they wrapped requests, maintaining symmetry (similar to middleware pattern in other frameworks).\n\n### Filter Wrapper Classes\n\nFilterManager wraps each filter in an `ActiveStreamFilterBase` subclass that manages iteration state:\n\n1. **ActiveStreamDecoderFilter** (filter_manager.h, lines 240–325)\n   - Wraps a `StreamDecoderFilter` (user-implemented filter)\n   - Maintains decoder-specific state and iteration control\n   - Implements `StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks` to provide filter callbacks (e.g., `continueDecoding()`, `sendLocalReply()`)\n\n2. **ActiveStreamEncoderFilter** (filter_manager.h, lines 330–end)\n   - Wraps a `StreamEncoderFilter`\n   - Manages encoder-specific state\n   - Implements `StreamEncoderFilterCallbacks`\n\nBoth inherit from `ActiveStreamFilterBase` which provides:\n- **Iteration State Management**: Tracks whether filter iteration is Continue, StopSingleIteration, or StopAll (with buffering)\n- **Filter Callbacks**: Connects each filter to the FilterManager for callbacks\n- **Status Handling**: Interprets filter return codes (FilterHeadersStatus, FilterDataStatus, etc.) and decides whether to continue or stop iteration\n\n### Filter Status Return Codes\n\nFilters return status codes that control iteration:\n\n| Status | Decoder Behavior | Encoder Behavior |\n|--------|------------------|------------------|\n| **Continue** | Iterate to next filter | Iterate to next filter |\n| **StopIteration** | Stop headers iteration; call `continueDecoding()` to resume | Stop headers iteration; caller must continue |\n| **StopAllIterationAndBuffer** | Stop all iteration and buffer following data until `continueDecoding()` | Stop all and buffer |\n| **ContinueAndDontEndStream** | Continue headers iteration but don't end stream (filter will inject data later) | — |\n\nWhen a filter returns `StopIteration`, the iteration state is recorded, and subsequent data frames call the same filter again rather than advancing to the next filter. Only when the filter calls `continueDecoding()` does iteration advance.\n\n### Filter Factory and Chain Creation\n\n`FilterChainFactory` (envoy/http/filter_factory.h) is invoked once per stream by ConnectionManagerImpl. It:\n\n1. Calls each filter factory function in order\n2. Each factory creates a filter instance and calls `addDecoderFilter()` or `addEncoderFilter()` on the callbacks object\n3. FilterManager appends these to its `StreamDecoderFilters` and `StreamEncoderFilters` lists\n\nThis allows dynamic filter creation based on route configuration, listener configuration, or other runtime state.\n\n### Data Buffering and Watermarks\n\nWhen a filter returns `StopAllIterationAndBuffer`:\n\n1. FilterManager allocates a buffer for subsequent data\n2. All subsequent data is appended to this buffer\n3. The filter is responsible for calling `continueDecoding()` or `continueEncoding()`\n4. When iteration resumes, the buffered data is replayed through the filter chain\n\nWatermarks prevent unbounded buffering:\n- If buffered data exceeds a configured limit, the connection signals high watermark\n- The upstream (or filter) is expected to slow down sending data\n- If high watermark is not respected and buffer exceeds hard limit, a 413 or 500 error is sent\n\n---\n\n## 3. Router Filter: Request Routing and Upstream Dispatch\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe Router Filter (`source/common/router/router.h/cc`) is the terminal decoder filter—it is always the last filter in the decoder chain. Its responsibilities are:\n\n1. **Route Selection**: Consult the route configuration to select a target cluster and route entry\n2. **Host Selection**: Use the cluster's load balancer to pick an upstream host\n3. **Connection Pool Allocation**: Obtain an HTTP connection pool from the ClusterManager\n4. **Upstream Request Creation**: Create and manage `UpstreamRequest` objects\n5. **Retry Logic**: Automatically retry failed requests based on route configuration\n6. **Timeout Management**: Set and enforce per-try and overall request timeouts\n7. **Shadow Routing**: Optionally send a copy of the request to a shadow cluster for testing\n8. **Hedged Requests**: Optionally send duplicate requests to different hosts for faster response\n\n### Route Selection\n\nWhen `Router::decodeHeaders()` is called:\n\n1. Extract route information from the request (headers, method, path, query parameters)\n2. Match against the configured `RouteConfiguration` (provided by RDS — Route Discovery Service)\n3. Retrieve the matching `RouteEntry` which specifies:\n   - **cluster**: The upstream cluster name\n   - **timeout**: Per-try and global timeout settings\n   - **retry_policy**: Conditions that trigger retries\n   - **shadow_policy**: Whether to shadow the request\n   - **weighted_clusters**: Alternative clusters to route to (canary deployments)\n\n### UpstreamRequest Lifecycle\n\nOnce a route is selected, the Router creates an `UpstreamRequest` object (source/common/router/upstream_request.h/cc):\n\n1. **Creation**: `std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>()` with a reference to the Router (parent) and a `GenericConnPool` from the ClusterManager.\n\n2. **Header Forwarding**: Router calls `acceptHeadersFromRouter()` on UpstreamRequest, which:\n   - Modifies headers (adds x-envoy headers, removes hop-by-hop headers)\n   - Passes the modified headers to the UpstreamRequest's internal `UpstreamFilterManager`\n   - The last filter in the upstream chain, `UpstreamCodecFilter`, attempts to encode headers to the upstream codec\n\n3. **Body Forwarding**: Subsequent `decodeData()` calls forward body data to UpstreamRequest\n\n4. **Upstream Connection Pool**: When the first header is forwarded, UpstreamRequest requests a connection from the pool. The ClusterManager allocates or reuses an existing HTTP connection pool.\n\n5. **Upstream Codec Bridge**: The `UpstreamCodecFilter` (source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.h/cc) maintains a `CodecBridge` that connects the upstream stream (from the upstream codec) back to the downstream FilterManager's encoder phase. When the upstream sends response headers, they are passed through the upstream filter chain (in reverse), then to the downstream encoder filter chain.\n\n6. **Retry Logic**: If the upstream connection fails or returns a retriable error (5xx status, connection reset), and `retry_policy` allows, Router creates a new UpstreamRequest and retries.\n\n7. **Completion**: When upstream sends trailers (end of response), UpstreamRequest signals completion. Router's encoder filters encode the response headers and body back downstream.\n\n### Router Filter Extensions\n\nRouter is itself extensible:\n\n- **Upstream HTTP Filters**: Similar to downstream filters, but run on the upstream request/response stream\n- **Shadow Writers**: Custom implementations can decide where to send shadow traffic\n- **Load Balancer Selection**: Through the cluster's load balancer interface\n\n---\n\n## 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity: Connection Pool Management\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ClusterManagerImpl` (source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h) manages all upstream clusters and their connection pools. It provides:\n\n1. **Cluster Registration**: Manages static clusters from the bootstrap config and dynamic clusters from CDS (Cluster Discovery Service)\n2. **Connection Pool Allocation**: Allocates HTTP/TCP connection pools per cluster per thread\n3. **Load Balancer Management**: Maintains load balancer instances per cluster\n4. **Health Checking**: Coordinates health checks and outlier detection\n5. **Thread-Local Storage**: Maintains thread-local cluster state for lock-free access\n\n### Connection Pool Architecture\n\nWhen Router calls `ClusterManager::httpConnPool()`:\n\n1. **Pool Lookup**: ClusterManager looks up a connection pool for the specified cluster, priority level, and protocol version\n2. **Pool Creation**: If no pool exists, it allocates one:\n   - For HTTP/1.1: `Http1ConnPool` (source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.h/cc)\n   - For HTTP/2: `Http2ConnPool` (source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.h/cc)\n   - For HTTP/3: `Http3ConnPool` (source/common/http/http3/conn_pool.h/cc)\n3. **Pool Callback**: Router registers itself as a connection pool callback\n4. **Connection Allocation**: When Router attempts to get a connection, the pool:\n   - Checks for idle connections in its internal pool\n   - If none available, allocates a new physical TCP/TLS connection\n   - Returns a handle to the connection\n\n### Load Balancing\n\nThe ClusterManager holds a reference to each cluster's load balancer. When Router needs a host:\n\n1. Creates a `LoadBalancerContext` containing:\n   - Request headers (for header-based routing)\n   - Upstream transport socket options\n   - Retry count (for retries)\n2. Calls `LoadBalancer::chooseHost(context)` to get an upstream host\n3. The load balancer applies:\n   - Health checks (unhealthy hosts are excluded)\n   - Outlier detection (hosts with too many errors are ejected)\n   - Load balancing algorithm (round-robin, least request, ring hash, etc.)\n   - Locality awareness (prefer hosts in the same zone/region)\n\n### Health Checking and Outlier Detection\n\nClusterManagerImpl integrates with health checking infrastructure:\n\n- **Health Checkers**: Each cluster can have multiple health check configurations (HTTP, TCP, gRPC)\n- **Outlier Detection**: Automatically ejects hosts that produce too many errors\n- **Load Balancer Integration**: The load balancer is notified when a host's health status changes, immediately removing unhealthy hosts from consideration\n\n### Cluster Discovery Service (CDS)\n\nClusters can be static (in bootstrap config) or dynamic (from CDS). ClusterManagerImpl:\n\n1. Maintains a CDS subscription via `CdsApi` (source/common/upstream/cds_api_impl.h/cc)\n2. When clusters are discovered, creates new Cluster objects and integrates them\n3. When clusters are updated, re-initializes connection pools and load balancers\n4. When clusters are removed, gracefully drains existing connections\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Request Through the System\n\n### Downstream Request Path\n\n```\n1. Network bytes arrive on TCP/TLS connection\n   ↓\n2. ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()\n   → Codec::dispatch() to decode bytes into HTTP frames\n   ↓\n3. Codec calls ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()\n   → ConnectionManagerImpl creates ActiveStream\n   → FilterChainFactory creates filter chain\n   → FilterManager is initialized\n   ↓\n4. Codec calls RequestDecoder::decodeHeaders()\n   → ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()\n   → FilterManager::decodeHeaders()\n   → Iterates through decoder filters: A → B → Router\n   ↓\n5. Codec calls RequestDecoder::decodeData()\n   → FilterManager::decodeData()\n   → Flows through same filter chain\n   ↓\n6. Codec calls RequestDecoder::decodeTrailers()\n   → FilterManager::decodeTrailers()\n   → Router is now at end of stream\n   ↓\n7. Router::decodeHeaders() selects route and cluster\n   → Obtains UpstreamRequest and GenericConnPool from ClusterManager\n   → Selects host using LoadBalancer\n   → Forwards headers to UpstreamRequest\n   ↓\n8. UpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter()\n   → Modifies headers (adds x-envoy headers, adjusts timeouts)\n   → UpstreamFilterManager processes upstream filter chain\n   → UpstreamCodecFilter encodes to upstream codec\n   → Codec connects to upstream host\n   ↓\n9. Upstream connection established\n   → Codec encodes headers to upstream\n```\n\n### Upstream Response Path\n\n```\n1. Upstream codec receives response headers\n   ↓\n2. UpstreamCodecFilter::CodecBridge::encodeHeaders()\n   → Response flows back through UpstreamFilterManager (reverse order)\n   → UpstreamRequest signals Router via decodeHeaders callback\n   ↓\n3. Router::encodeHeaders() is invoked\n   → Encoder filters iterate in reverse order: Router → B → A\n   → Each encoder filter can modify or inspect response\n   ↓\n4. Response data flows upstream → downstream\n   → UpstreamCodecFilter receives data from upstream\n   → Router forwards to ActiveStream::encodeData()\n   → FilterManager iterates encoder filters\n   ↓\n5. Response trailers arrive\n   → Same flow through encoder filter chain\n   ↓\n6. FilterManager::encodeTrailers() completes\n   → Codec encodes all response data to downstream connection\n   ↓\n7. Downstream receives full response\n   → ActiveStream marks stream complete\n   → AccessLogger is invoked\n   → Stream is deferred-deleted\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points: Where Users Extend Envoy\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\nUsers implement `StreamDecoderFilter` or `StreamEncoderFilter` (envoy/http/filter.h) to:\n\n- Inspect or modify request/response headers\n- Inspect or modify request/response body\n- Perform authentication/authorization\n- Add tracing\n- Implement custom routing logic (via `sendLocalReply()` to terminate early)\n- Buffer and delay streams\n\nFilters are registered via the filter factory pattern and instantiated per stream.\n\n### 2. Upstream Filters\n\nSimilar to HTTP filters, but apply to the upstream request/response. Used for:\n\n- Modifying upstream-specific headers\n- Compression/decompression\n- Custom upstream request/response handling\n\n### 3. Load Balancer Implementations\n\nUsers implement `LoadBalancer` (envoy/upstream/load_balancer.h) to:\n\n- Implement custom load balancing algorithms (consistent hashing, power-of-two, etc.)\n- Use custom routing criteria from request context\n- Integrate with external load balancing services\n\n### 4. Health Checkers\n\nUsers implement health check plugins to:\n\n- Perform custom health checks (application-specific protocols)\n- Integrate with external health check systems\n\n### 5. Cluster Types\n\nUsers implement `Cluster` (envoy/upstream/cluster.h) to:\n\n- Define custom cluster behavior (aggregate multiple endpoint sources, etc.)\n- Implement custom endpoint discovery mechanisms\n\n### 6. Access Loggers\n\nUsers implement `AccessLog` (envoy/access_log/access_log.h) to:\n\n- Log detailed request/response information\n- Send logs to custom destinations (metrics systems, log aggregators)\n- Trigger alerts based on response codes or latency\n\nAccess loggers are invoked when a stream completes and have access to:\n- All request headers, body, trailers\n- All response headers, body, trailers\n- Duration, bytes sent/received, status codes\n- Cluster info, upstream host info\n- Custom stream-specific state (filter state)\n\n### 7. Filter State\n\nFilters and custom code can store arbitrary state in `StreamInfo::FilterState` (envoy/stream_info/filter_state.h) for:\n\n- Passing data between filters\n- Making data available to access loggers\n- Sharing custom context across the request lifecycle\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Codec Errors\n\nIf the downstream codec encounters a malformed HTTP message:\n\n1. Codec reports error via `ServerConnectionCallbacks::onCodecError()` or similar\n2. ConnectionManagerImpl sends a 400 Bad Request response (or closes connection)\n3. Stream is terminated and cleaned up\n\n### Filter Errors\n\nIf a filter encounters an error and calls `sendLocalReply()`:\n\n1. FilterManager stops iteration of remaining filters\n2. Encoder filters are still executed to allow them to modify the error response\n3. The local reply (error) is encoded to the downstream connection\n4. Stream completes with error status\n\n### Upstream Connection Errors\n\nIf the upstream connection fails during request forwarding:\n\n1. UpstreamRequest detects connection reset or timeout\n2. Router's retry logic consults `retry_policy`\n3. If retriable, creates new UpstreamRequest with incremented retry count\n4. Selects new host via load balancer\n5. If all retries exhausted, sends 503 or upstream error response\n\n### Timeout Errors\n\nTwo levels of timeouts:\n\n1. **Per-Try Timeout**: Timeout per attempt to reach upstream. If exceeded, triggers retry if configured.\n2. **Global Timeout**: Total time allowed for request (across all retries). If exceeded, sends 504 Gateway Timeout.\n\nBoth timeouts are managed by UpstreamRequest and Router, using the Event Dispatcher's timer mechanism.\n\n### Stream Reset\n\nIf a stream is reset mid-processing (client disconnect, filter error):\n\n1. ActiveStream::onResetStream() is called\n2. Any pending UpstreamRequest is cleaned up\n3. Downstream encoder is stopped\n4. Stream is deferred-deleted\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files Reference\n\n### Core Connection Management\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` — ConnectionManagerImpl class, ActiveStream struct\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_config.h` — Configuration for connection manager\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_utility.h` — Utility functions\n\n### Filter Chain Execution\n- RequestDecoder, ResponseEncoder)\n\n### Router Filter\n- `source/common/router/router.h` — Router filter class\n- `source/common/router/upstream_request.h` — UpstreamRequest class for per-request upstream management\n- `source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.h` — UpstreamCodecFilter and CodecBridge\n- `source/common/router/config_impl.h` — RouteConfiguration and route matching\n- interface\n\n### Interfaces and Abstractions\n- `envoy/http/header_map.h` — HTTP header container interface\n- `envoy/network/filter.h` — Network filter base class (inherited by ConnectionManagerImpl)\n- `envoy/stream_info/stream_info.h` — StreamInfo interface for accessing request/response metadata\n- `envoy/access_log/access_log.h` — Access logger interface\n- `envoy/router/rds.h` — Route discovery service interface\n\n---\n\n## Summary: Component Interactions\n\nThe four major components interact as follows:\n\n1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** receives raw bytes and creates an HTTP codec. When a new HTTP stream is detected, it instantiates an **ActiveStream** and delegates to **FilterChainFactory** to build the filter chain.\n\n2. **FilterManager** iterates through the decoder filter chain as request data arrives. Filters can modify, inspect, or stop iteration.\n\n3. **Router Filter** is the terminal decoder filter. It selects a route from the **ClusterManager**, creates an **UpstreamRequest**, and begins forwarding the request.\n\n4. **ClusterManager** provides connection pools and selects hosts via load balancers. It manages the lifecycle of upstream connections.\n\nThe response flows back through **UpstreamRequest** (which runs upstream filters), then through **ActiveStream** (which runs downstream encoder filters), and finally the **Codec** encodes the response bytes to the client.\n\nThroughout this process:\n- **Filters** at any stage can send local replies to short-circuit the chain\n- **Status codes** control iteration behavior (continue, stop and buffer, etc.)\n- **Timeouts** and **retries** are managed by the router\n- **Access loggers** are invoked when the stream completes\n- **Custom state** can be stored in FilterState for cross-filter communication\n\nThis architecture enables Envoy's flexibility: users can insert custom filters at any point, implement custom load balancers, extend codec behavior, and integrate custom health checks—all without modifying Envoy's core request processing loop.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

It is a complex orchestration of multiple interdependent components that work together to:\n\n1. Accept raw network bytes from downstream connections\n2. Decode HTTP frames using protocol-specific codecs (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3)\n3. Execute a chain of filters that can inspect, modify, or intercept the request\n4. Route the request to an appropriate upstream cluster\n5. Manage upstream connections and retry logic\n6. Encode the upstream response back to the downstream client\n\nThis document explains how the four primary components of the HCM interact to achieve this goal.\n\n---\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: The Central Request Orchestrator\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc) is the top-level filter in Envoy's network filter stack. It implements:\n\n- **Network::ReadFilter** — receives raw bytes from the downstream connection\n- **ServerConnectionCallbacks** — receives callbacks from the HTTP codec when new streams are created\n- **Network::ConnectionCallbacks** — manages the lifecycle of the underlying TCP/TLS connection\n- **Http::ApiListener** — allows direct HTTP request injection (for API listeners, not socket-based)\n\n### Key Responsibilities\n\n1. **Codec Management**: Creates and maintains an HTTP codec (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, or HTTP/3) lazily or on-demand. The codec is protocol-agnostic internally; ConnectionManagerImpl treats it as a black box that decodes bytes into HTTP frames and encodes HTTP frames back to bytes.\n\n2. **Stream Lifecycle**: For each incoming HTTP request, creates an `ActiveStream` object that wraps the stream and manages its state from arrival through completion. These streams are organized in a linked list for efficient management during connection shutdown or drain.\n\n3. **Filter Chain Creation**: When a new stream arrives, delegates to `FilterChainFactory` to create the per-stream filter chain (detailed below).\n\n4. **Connection-Level Concerns**:\n   - **Drain Decisions**: Monitors connection drain signals and prevents new streams on draining connections (graceful shutdown)\n   - **Overload Management**: Checks with `OverloadManager` to decide whether to accept new connections\n   - **Watermark-Based Flow Control**: Propagates buffer watermark events from the underlying connection to all active streams to manage memory usage\n\n5. **Stream Completion**: When a stream finishes, ensures proper cleanup, logging (via access loggers), and deferred deletion to avoid lifetime issues.\n\n### ActiveStream: Per-Stream State Wrapper\n\n`ActiveStream` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h, lines 141–end of private section) is a critical internal struct that:\n\n- Wraps a single HTTP request/response pair\n- Owns the `FilterManager` that executes the filter chain for this specific stream\n- Implements `RequestDecoder` to receive decoded HTTP frames (headers, data, trailers)","numLines":50,"startLine":1,"totalLines":554}}}
